BIB                 20        104                                 22884  1    2 
TITLE       Light charged particle emission induced by fast       22884  1    3 
            neutrons with energies between 25 and 65 MeV on iron  22884  1    4 
AUTHOR     (I.Slypen,N.Nica,A.Koning,E.Raeymackers,S.Benck,       22884  1    5 
            J.P.Meulders,V.Corcalciuc)                            22884  1    6 
INSTITUTE  (2BLGLVN) Slypen, Nica, Raeymackers, Benck, Meulders   22884  1    7 
           (3RUMBUC) Nica, Corcalciuc                             22884  1    8 
           (2NEDNRG) Nica, Koning, Nuclear Research and           22884  1    9 
                     Consultancy Group NRG, Petten, Netherlands   22884  1   10 
REFERENCE  (J,JP/G,30,45,2004)    Main reference,cross sections   22884  1   11 
            were superseded by data from At.Data&Nucl.Data Tabl.8722884  1   12 
           (J,AND,87,231,2004)     Final numerical data set       22884  1   13 
                                for natural iron in Table 1       22884  1   14 
REL-REF    (M,22810001,N.Nica+,J,JP/G,28,2823,2002)  Data         22884  1   15 
            analysis details                                      22884  1   16 
           (M,22807001,S.Benck+,J,NSE,141,(1),55,2002)  Exp.      22884  1   17 
                                         details, error structure 22884  1   18 
           (I,,I.Slypen+,J,NIM/A,337,431,1994) Experim. details   22884  1   19 
           (M,,I.Slypen+,J,NIM/B,88,275,1994) - thick target      22884  1   20 
           correction procedure by Monte Carlo simulation program 22884  1   21 
           (I,,A.Bol+,J,NIM,214,169,1983)  Description of the     22884  1   22 
                 CYCLONE facility                                 22884  1   23 
FACILITY   (CYCLO,2BLGLVN)  Fast neutron facility cyclotron       22884  1   24 
                            'CYCLONE'                             22884  1   25 
INC-SOURCE (P-LI7)  65 MeV proton beam strikes 3 mm thick         22884  1   26 
             natural lithium target. proton current is 12 micro-A 22884  1   27 
             producing ~1.0E+5 neutrons/cm2/sec at the location   22884  1   28 
             of the target                                        22884  1   29 
INC-SPECT   Full width at half-maximum is ~2 MeV containing       22884  1   30 
            90% of neutrons/MeV plus a flat continuum of          22884  1   31 
            low-energy neutrons.                                  22884  1   32 
           -For energy calibration the proton and deuteron recoi- 22884  1   33 
            ling from respectively a polypropylene (1 mm thick)   22884  1   34 
            and deuterated polypropylene target (0.6 mm thick)    22884  1   35 
            were used.                                            22884  1   36 
           (EN-RSL) -half width of the incident neutron energy bin22884  1   37 
DETECTOR   (COIN,TELES,SCIN,CSICR)  Four charged particles        22884  1   38 
             detector consisting of six telescopes were used      22884  1   39 
             simultaneously, each of them consists of             22884  1   40 
             1.  'Delta-E' Detector NE102 plastic scintillator,   22884  1   41 
                  0.1 mm thick, 4 cm in diameter, and             22884  1   42 
             2.   Cs-I(TL) 'E' detector, crystal 22 mm thick,     22884  1   43 
                  38.1 mm in diameter                             22884  1   44 
METHOD     (TOF)  The time-of-flight was deduced from the         22884  1   45 
              time difference between the capacitive beam pickoff 22884  1   46 
              located upstream from the neutron-producing target, 22884  1   47 
              and the delta-E detector. only those events of      22884  1   48 
              charged particles detection  were registered which  22884  1   49 
              are associated with neutrons in the main neutron    22884  1   50 
              peak.                                               22884  1   51 
           (COINC,EDE)                                            22884  1   52 
ANALYSIS    Interpolation and extrapolation of double-differential22884  1   53 
            data was performed with the help of two-parameter     22884  1   54 
            formula a*exp(b*cos(theta)), theta is angle of scatte-22884  1   55 
            ring in lab. system                                   22884  1   56 
MONITOR    (1-H-1(N,EL)1-H-1,,DA)   Cross sections were measured  22884  1   57 
             at degrees between 20 and 70 degree with step 10 deg,22884  1   58 
             110, 140 and 160 degree in each of the telescopes    22884  1   59 
MONIT-REF  (,S.Benck+,J,NP/A,615,220,1997)                        22884  1   60 
SAMPLE      Natural iron target 0.5 mm thick, 6*6 cm2 surface,    22884  1   61 
            density 2.4 gram/cm2                                  22884  1   62 
CORRECTION  The solid angle and thick target corrections were     22884  1   63 
            made with the help of Monte Carlo simulation program  22884  1   64 
ADD-RES    (THEO,COMP)  GNASH and TALYS codes were used for light 22884  1   65 
              charged particles cross sections evaluation.        22884  1   66 
           The iron data are also compared with previously        22884  1   67 
           published cobalt results (see Entry 22810).            22884  1   68 
ERR-ANALYS (ERR-T) Total error includes ERR-SYS and DATA-ERR      22884  1   69 
             (as it is given in thesis)                           22884  1   70 
           (ERR-SYS,7.,8.) uncertainty of the cross section       22884  1   71 
            absolute scale due to:                                22884  1   72 
           (ERR-1) uncertainty in the measured reference (n,p)    22884  1   73 
                  cross sections (5%),                            22884  1   74 
           (ERR-2) uncertainty in the beam monitoring (2%),       22884  1   75 
           (ERR-3,2.,5.) uncertainty in the statistics in the     22884  1   76 
                         H(n,p) recoil proton peak (2-5%),        22884  1   77 
           (ERR-4) uncertainty in solid angle corrections (1%),   22884  1   78 
           (ERR-5) uncertainty in number of target nuclei, etc.   22884  1   79 
           (DATA-ERR,5.5) The overall relative uncertainties of   22884  1   80 
           the experimental points in the spectra are about 5.5%, 22884  1   81 
           8.5%, 15.% and 25% for respectively p, d, t and alpha  22884  1   82 
           at 62.7 MeV. They are mainly given by the statistics   22884  1   83 
           in the spectra. At lower ejectile energies, the thick  22884  1   84 
           target corrections contribute with supplementary       22884  1   85 
           uncertainties. For all the other incident neutron      22884  1   86 
           energies (continuum), these values are between 2 and 3 22884  1   87 
           times higher as a consequence of the lower incident    22884  1   88 
           neutron flux.                                          22884  1   89

           than the values in J.Phys.G30(2004)45-64               22884  1   92
